        if(maxi%l[i]!=0):
            return False
    return True

                cursor.execute(f'insert into {database_name}.car values ("{c[0]}","{c[1]}","{c[2]}","{c[3]}","{c[4]}","{c[5]}","{c[6]}")')
                mydb.commit()
        print("all data inserted")
        print(count)
except Exception as e:
    print(str(e))

30/03/22, 9:27 am - +91 94309 18870: Write a function that sorts a list of integers by their digit length in descending order, then settles ties by sorting numbers with the same digit length in ascending order.
Examples

digit_sort([77, 23, 5, 7, 101]) â [101, 23, 77, 5, 7]

digit_sort([1, 5, 9, 2, 789, 563, 444]) â [444, 563, 789, 1, 2, 5, 9]

digit_sort([53219, 3772, 564, 32, 1]) â [53219, 3772, 564, 32, 1]























# Approach_1:

def digit_sort_1(lst):
    
    output = sorted(lst, key = lambda i : (-len(str(i)),i))
    print(f'digit_sort({lst}) â {output}')
    
digit_sort_1([77, 23, 5, 7, 101])
digit_sort_1([1, 5, 9, 2, 789, 563, 444])
digit_sort_1([53219, 3772, 564, 32, 1])



print()
# Approach_2:

def digit_sort_2(lst):
    
    output = sorted(lst, key = lambda i : (len(str(i)),-i),reverse = True)
    print(f'digit_sort({lst}) â {output}')
    
digit_sort_2([77, 23, 5, 7, 101])
digit_sort_2([1, 5, 9, 2, 789, 563, 444])
digit_sort_2([53219, 3772, 564, 32, 1])
